   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Maldives</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Island country in the Indian Ocean southwest of India and Sri Lanka
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Islas Malvinas (Falkland Islands)</a>.
      </div>

         <td>1,102.5/km<sup>2</sup> (2,855.5/sq&nbsp;mi) (<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population_density" title="List of countries and dependencies by population density">11th</a>)</td>

      <p><b>Maldives</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">ɔː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">ɔː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Dhivehi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhivehi language">Dhivehi</a>: <span lang="dv" dir="rtl">ދިވެހިރާއްޖެ</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Dhivehi" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanization of Dhivehi">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="dv-Latn" title="Dhivehi-language romanization">Dhivehi Raajje</i>), officially the <b>Republic of Maldives</b>, is a small <a href="/wiki/Archipelagic_state" title="Archipelagic state">archipelagic state</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>, situated in the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>. It lies southwest of <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, about 700 kilometres (430&nbsp;mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> continent's mainland. The chain of <a href="/wiki/Atolls_of_the_Maldives" title="Atolls of the Maldives">26 atolls</a> stretches from <a href="/wiki/Atolls_of_the_Maldives#Ihavandhippolhu" title="Atolls of the Maldives">Ihavandhippolhu Atoll</a> in the north to <a href="/wiki/Addu_Atoll" title="Addu Atoll">Addu Atoll</a> in the south (across the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>). Comprising a <a href="/wiki/Territory" title="Territory">territory</a> spanning roughly 298 square kilometres (115&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), Maldives is one of the world's most geographically dispersed <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Asia" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in Asia">smallest Asian country</a> by land area and, with around 557,426 inhabitants, the 2nd <a href="/wiki/List_of_Asian_countries_by_population" title="List of Asian countries by population">least populous country in Asia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9" title="Malé">Malé</a> is the capital and the most populated city, traditionally called the "King's Island" where the ancient <a href="/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Maldives" title="List of sultans of the Maldives">royal dynasties</a> ruled for its central location.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Maldivian Archipelago is located on the <a href="/wiki/Chagos-Laccadive_Ridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Chagos-Laccadive Ridge">Chagos-Laccadive Ridge</a>, a vast submarine mountain range in the Indian Ocean; this also forms a <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion#Terrestrial" title="Ecoregion">terrestrial ecoregion</a>, together with the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lakshadweep" title="Lakshadweep">Lakshadweep</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> With an average ground-level elevation of 1.5 metres (4&nbsp;ft 11&nbsp;in) above sea level,<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-15">[15]</a></sup> it is the world's lowest-lying country, with even its <a href="/wiki/List_of_elevation_extremes_by_country" title="List of elevation extremes by country">highest natural point</a> being one of the lowest in the world, at 5.1 metres (17&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 12th century <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> reached the Maldivian Archipelago, which was consolidated as a <a href="/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Maldives" title="List of sultans of the Maldives">sultanate</a>, developing strong commercial and cultural ties with <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. From the mid-16th-century the region came under the increasing influence of European <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial powers</a>, with Maldives becoming a British <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> in 1887. <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Maldives#Independence" title="History of the Maldives">Independence</a> from the United Kingdom came in 1965, and a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential republic</a> was established in 1968 with an elected <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Majlis" title="People's Majlis">People's Majlis</a>. The ensuing decades have seen political instability, efforts at democratic reform,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and environmental challenges posed by <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Maldives became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation</a> (SAARC). It is also a member of the United Nations, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. The World Bank classifies the Maldives as having an upper-<a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">middle income</a> economy.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry_in_the_Maldives" title="Fishing industry in the Maldives">Fishing</a> has historically been the dominant economic activity, and remains the largest sector by far, followed by the rapidly growing <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_the_Maldives" title="Tourism in the Maldives">tourism</a> industry. Maldives rate "high" on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HDI_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDI-12">[12]</a></sup> with per-capita income significantly higher than other SAARC nations.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Maldives was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> from July 1982 until withdrawing from the organisation in October 2016 in protest at allegations by the other nations of its <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> abuses and failing democracy. The Maldives rejoined the Commonwealth on 1 February 2020 after showing evidence of functioning democratic processes and popular support. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

                <td class="mbox-image">
                 <div style="width:52px">
                  <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>

             <table class="box-Original_research plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Original_research" role="presentation">

                <td class="mbox-image">
                 <div style="width:52px">
                  <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40">

                <td class="mbox-text">
                 <div class="mbox-text-span">
                  This section <b>possibly contains <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research">original research</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verifying</a> the claims made and adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">inline citations</a>.                  </div></td>
               </tr>
              </tbody>
             </table> 
            </div> 
           </div><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>According to legends, the first settlers of Maldives were people known as Dheyvis.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> The first Kingdom of the Maldives was known as Dheeva Maari. In the 3rd century BC during the visit of emissaries sent by Emperor Asoka, Maldives was known as Dheeva Mahal.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During c. 1100 - 1166, Maldives was also referred as Diva Kudha and the Laccadive archipelago which was a part of Maldives was then referred to as Diva Khanbar by the scholar and polymath <a href="/wiki/Al-Biruni" title="Al-Biruni">al-Biruni</a> (973-1048).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The name <i>Maldives</i> may also derive from <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> <i><i lang="sa-Latn" title="Sanskrit-language text">mālā</i></i> (garland) and <i><i lang="sa-Latn" title="Sanskrit-language text">dvīpa</i></i> (island),<sup id="cite_ref-Hogendorn_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hogendorn-23">[23]</a></sup> or <span lang="si" title="Sinhala-language text">මාල දිවයින</span> <i>Maala Divaina</i> ("Necklace Islands") in <a href="/wiki/Sinhala_language" title="Sinhala language">Sinhala</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ParanavitanaPrematilleka1978_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParanavitanaPrematilleka1978-24">[24]</a></sup> The Maldivian people are called <i>Dhivehin</i>. The word <i>Dheeb/Deeb</i> (archaic <i>Dhivehi</i>, related to <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> <span lang="sa" title="Sanskrit-language text">द्वीप</span>, <i><i lang="sa-Latn" title="Sanskrit-language text">dvīpa</i></i>) means "island", and <i>Dhives</i> (<i>Dhivehin</i>) means "islanders" (i.e., Maldivians).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The ancient <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lankan</a> chronicle <i><a href="/wiki/Mahawamsa" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahawamsa">Mahawamsa</a></i> refers to an island called <i>Mahiladiva</i> ("Island of Women", महिलादिभ) in <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">Pali</a>, which is probably a mistranslation of the same Sanskrit word meaning "<a href="/wiki/Garland" title="Garland">garland</a>". </p>
      <p>Jan Hogendorn, Grossman Professor of Economics,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)"><span title="The geographic scope near this tag is ambiguous. (September 2019)">where?</span></a></i>]</sup> theorises that the name Maldives derives from the Sanskrit <i><i lang="sa-Latn" title="Sanskrit-language text">mālādvīpa</i></i> (<span lang="sa" title="Sanskrit-language text">मालाद्वीप</span>), meaning "garland of islands".<sup id="cite_ref-Hogendorn_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hogendorn-23">[23]</a></sup> In Tamil, "Garland of Islands" can be translated as <i><i lang="ta-Latn" title="Tamil-language text">Malai Theevu</i></i> (<span lang="ta" title="Tamil-language text">மாலைத்தீவு</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a>, "Garland of Islands" can be translated as <i><i lang="ml-Latn" title="Malayalam-language text">Maladweepu</i></i> (<span lang="ml" title="Malayalam-language text">മാലദ്വീപ്</span>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In Kannada, "Garland of Islands" can be translated as <i><i lang="kn-Latn" title="Kannada-language text">Maaledweepa</i></i> (<span lang="kn" title="Kannada-language text">ಮಾಲೆದ್ವೀಪ</span>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> None of these names is mentioned in any literature,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> but classical Sanskrit texts dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Vedic_period" title="Vedic period">Vedic period</a> mention the "Hundred Thousand Islands" (<i><i lang="sa-Latn" title="Sanskrit-language text"><a href="/wiki/Lakshadweep" title="Lakshadweep">Lakshadweepa</a></i></i>), a generic name which would include not only the Maldives, but also the <a href="/wiki/Laccadives" class="mw-redirect" title="Laccadives">Laccadives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aminidivi" title="Aminidivi">Aminidivi</a> Islands, <a href="/wiki/Minicoy" title="Minicoy">Minicoy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos island</a> groups.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (September 2019)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Some medieval travellers such as <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Battuta" title="Ibn Battuta">Ibn Battuta</a> called the islands <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language text">Mahal Dibiyat</i></i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic-language text">محل دبيأت</span>) from the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> word <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language text">mahal</i></i> ("palace"), which must be how the <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Berber</a> traveller interpreted the local name, having been through Muslim North India, where <a href="/wiki/Perso-Arabic" class="mw-redirect" title="Perso-Arabic">Perso-Arabic</a> words were introduced to the local vocabulary.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> This is the name currently inscribed on the scroll in the <a href="/wiki/Emblem_of_Maldives" title="Emblem of Maldives">Maldive state emblem</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The classical Persian/Arabic name for Maldives is <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language text">Dibajat</i></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The Dutch referred to the islands as the <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Maldivische Eilanden</i></i> (<small>pronounced </small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[mɑlˈdivisə ˈʔɛilɑndə(n)]</a></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-WWW.IBPUS.COM_69_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WWW.IBPUS.COM_69-31">[31]</a></sup> while the British <a href="/wiki/Anglicisation" title="Anglicisation">anglicised</a> the local name for the islands first to the "Maldive Islands" and later to "Maldives".<sup id="cite_ref-WWW.IBPUS.COM_69_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WWW.IBPUS.COM_69-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Garcia da Orta writes in a conversational book first published in 1563, writes as follows: "I must tell you that I have heard it said that the natives do not call it Maldiva but Nalediva. In the Malabar language <i>nale</i> means four and <i>diva</i> island. So that in that language the word signifies "four islands," while we, corrupting the name, call it Maldiva."<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Maldives" title="History of the Maldives">History of the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_history_and_settlement">Ancient history and settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient history and settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Maldives#Early_Age" title="History of the Maldives">History of the Maldives §&nbsp;Early Age</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Maldives is an old nation, well over 2,500 years old according to legends of the southern atolls. </p>
      <p>According to the book "Kitāb fi āthār Mīdhu al-qādimah (كتاب في آثار ميذو القديمة) ("On the Ancient Ruins of <a href="/wiki/Meedhoo_(Addu)" class="mw-redirect" title="Meedhoo (Addu)">Meedhoo</a>")" written in the 17th century in Arabic by Allama Ahmed Shihabuddine (Allama Shihab al-Din) of <a href="/wiki/Meedhoo_(Addu)" class="mw-redirect" title="Meedhoo (Addu)">Meedhoo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Addu_Atoll" title="Addu Atoll">Addu Atoll</a>, the first settlers of the Maldives were people known as Dheyvis.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> They came from the <a href="/wiki/Kalibangan" title="Kalibangan">Kalibanga</a> in India.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> The time of their arrival is unknown but it was before Emperor <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Asoka</a>'s kingdom in 269-232 BC. Shihabuddine's story tallies remarkably well with the recorded history of South Asia and that of copperplate document of Maldives known as <a href="/wiki/L%C5%8Dm%C4%81f%C4%81nu" title="Lōmāfānu">Loamaafaanu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i>Maapanansa</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-:12_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-21">[21]</a></sup> the copper plates on which was recorded the history of the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Maldives" title="List of sultans of the Maldives">Kings of Maldives</a> from the Solar Dynasty, were lost quite early on. </p>
      <p>A 4th-century notice written by <a href="/wiki/Ammianus_Marcellinus" title="Ammianus Marcellinus">Ammianus Marcellinus</a> (362 AD) speaks of gifts sent to the Roman emperor <a href="/wiki/Julian_(emperor)" title="Julian (emperor)">Julian</a> by a deputation from the nation of Divi. The name Divi is very similar to Dheyvi who were the first settlers of Maldives.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The ancient history of Maldives is told in copperplates, ancients scripts carved on coral artifacts, traditions, language and different ethnicities of Maldivians.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first Maldivians did not leave any archaeological artifacts. Their buildings were probably built of wood, palm fronds, and other perishable materials, which would have quickly decayed in the salt and wind of the tropical climate. Moreover, chiefs or headmen did not reside in elaborate stone palaces, nor did their religion require the construction of large temples or compounds.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Comparative studies of Maldivian oral, linguistic, and cultural traditions confirm that the first settlers were people from the southern shores of the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-34">[34]</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/Giraavaru_people" title="Giraavaru people">Giraavaru people</a>, mentioned in ancient legends and local folklore about the establishment of the capital and kingly rule in <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9" title="Malé">Malé</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A strong underlying layer of <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_peoples" title="Dravidian peoples">Dravidian</a> population and culture survives in Maldivian society, with a clear <a href="/wiki/Tamil%E2%80%93Kannada_languages" title="Tamil–Kannada languages">Tamil-Malayalam</a> substratum in the language, which also appears in place names, kinship terms, poetry, dance, and religious beliefs. <a href="/wiki/Malabar_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Malabar region">Malabar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pandyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Pandyan">Pandya</a> seafaring culture led to the settlement of the Islands by <a href="/wiki/Tamils" title="Tamils">Tamil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malabars" title="Malabars">Malabar</a> seafarers.<sup id="cite_ref-Maloney,_Clarence_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maloney,_Clarence-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Maldive Islands were mentioned in Ancient Sangam Tamil Literature as "Munneer Pazhantheevam" or "Older Islands of Three Seas". </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buddhist_period">Buddhist period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Buddhist period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Maldives#Buddhist_period" title="History of the Maldives">History of the Maldives §&nbsp;Buddhist period</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_the_Maldives" title="Buddhism in the Maldives">Buddhism in the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Loamaafaanu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e6/Loamaafaanu.jpg/220px-Loamaafaanu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e6/Loamaafaanu.jpg/330px-Loamaafaanu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e6/Loamaafaanu.jpg/440px-Loamaafaanu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1432" data-file-height="1075"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Loamaafaanu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Isdhoo_(Laamu_Atoll)" title="Isdhoo (Laamu Atoll)">Isdhoo</a> Lōmāfānu is the oldest <a href="/wiki/L%C5%8Dm%C4%81f%C4%81nu" title="Lōmāfānu">copper-plate</a> book to have been discovered in the Maldives to date. The book was written in AD 1194 (590 AH) in the Evēla form of the <a href="/wiki/Dhivehi_Writing_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhivehi Writing Systems">Divehi akuru</a>, during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Dhinei_of_the_Maldives" title="Dhinei of the Maldives">Siri Fennaadheettha Mahaa Radun (Dhinei Kalaminja)</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite being just mentioned briefly in most history books, the 1,400-year-long Buddhist period has foundational importance in the history of the Maldives. It was during this period that the culture of the Maldives both developed and flourished, a culture which survives today. The Maldivian <a href="/wiki/Dhivehi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhivehi language">language</a>, early Maldive <a href="/wiki/Dhivehi_Writing_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhivehi Writing Systems">scripts</a>, architecture, ruling institutions, customs, and manners of the Maldivians originated at the time when the Maldives were a Buddhist kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Buddhism probably spread to the Maldives in the 3rd century BC at the time of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Ashoka</a>'s expansion and became the dominant religion of the people of the Maldives until the 12th century AD. The ancient Maldivian Kings promoted <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, and the first Maldive writings and artistic achievements, in the form of highly developed sculpture and architecture, originate from that period. Nearly all archaeological remains in the Maldives are from Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Stupa" title="Stupa">stupas</a> and monasteries, and all artifacts found to date display characteristic Buddhist iconography. </p>
      <p>Buddhist (and Hindu) temples were <a href="/wiki/Mandala" title="Mandala">Mandala</a> shaped. They are oriented according to the four cardinal points with the main gate facing east. Local historian Hassan Ahmed Maniku counted as many as 59 islands with Buddhist archaeological sites in a provisional list he published in 1990. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_period">Islamic period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Islamic period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Maldives#Islamic_Period" title="History of the Maldives">History of the Maldives §&nbsp;Islamic Period</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Maldives" class="mw-redirect" title="Islam in Maldives">Islam in Maldives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Maldives" title="List of sultans of the Maldives">List of sultans of the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The importance of the Arabs as traders in the Indian Ocean by the 12th century may partly explain why the last Buddhist king of Maldives, <a href="/wiki/Dhovemi_of_the_Maldives" title="Dhovemi of the Maldives">Dhovemi</a>, converted to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> in the year 1153 (or 1193). Adopting the Muslim title of Sultan Muhammad ibn Abdullah, he initiated a series of six Islamic dynasties that lasted until 1932 when the sultanate became elective. The formal title of the sultan up to 1965 was, <i>Sultan of Land and Sea, Lord of the twelve-thousand islands and Sultan of the Maldives</i> which came with the style <i><a href="/wiki/Highness" title="Highness">Highness</a></i>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somali</a> Muslim Abu al-Barakat Yusuf al-Barbari, also known as <a href="/wiki/Aw_Barkhadle" class="mw-redirect" title="Aw Barkhadle">Aw Barkhadle</a>, is traditionally credited for this conversion. According to the story told to <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Battutah" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibn Battutah">Ibn Battutah</a>, a mosque was built with the inscription: 'The Sultan Ahmad Shanurazah accepted Islam at the hand of Abu al-Barakat Yusuf al-Barbari.'<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Some scholars have suggested the possibility of Ibn Battuta misreading Maldive texts, and having a bias towards the North African, Maghrebi narrative of this Shaykh, instead of the East African origins account that was known as well at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Even when Ibn Battuta visited the islands, the governor of the island at that time was <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Aziz_of_Mogadishu" title="Abd al-Aziz of Mogadishu">Abd Aziz Al Mogadishawi</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somali</a><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Scholars have posited another scenario where Abu al-Barakat Yusuf al-Barbari might have been a native of <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Barbera</a>, a significant trading port on the northwestern coast of <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <i>Barbara</i> or <i>Barbaroi</i> (Berbers), as the ancestors of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali people">Somalis</a> were referred to by medieval <a href="/wiki/Arab_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab people">Arab</a> and ancient <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a> geographers, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Bagley222_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bagley222-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mohamed_Diriye_Abdullahi_2001_p.1322_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mohamed_Diriye_Abdullahi_2001_p.1322-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> This is also seen when Ibn Batuta visited <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a>, he mentions that the Sultan at that time, "Abu Bakr ibn Shaikh Omar", was a Berber (Somali). According to scholars, Abu al-Barakat Yusuf al-Barbari was <a href="/wiki/Yusuf_bin_Ahmad_al-Kawneyn" title="Yusuf bin Ahmad al-Kawneyn">Yusuf bin Ahmad al-Kawneyn</a>, a famous native <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somali</a> scholar<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> known for establishing the <a href="/wiki/Walashma_dynasty" title="Walashma dynasty">Walashma dynasty</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> After his conversion of the population of Dogor (now known as <a href="/wiki/Aw_Barkhadle" class="mw-redirect" title="Aw Barkhadle">Aw Barkhadle</a>), a town in Somalia, he is also credited to have been responsible for spreading Islam in the Maldivian islands, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9_Friday_Mosque" title="Malé Friday Mosque">Hukuru Miskiy</a>, and converting the Maldivian population to Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Batuta" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibn Batuta">Ibn Batuta</a> states the Maldivian king was converted by Abu al-Barakat Yusuf al-Barbari (Blessed Father of Somalia).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Others have it he may have been from the Persian town of <a href="/wiki/Tabriz" title="Tabriz">Tabriz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The first reference to an Iranian origin dates to an 18th-century Persian text.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>His venerated tomb now stands on the grounds of Medhu Ziyaaraiy, across the street from the Friday Mosque, or <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9_Friday_Mosque" title="Malé Friday Mosque">Hukuru Miskiy</a>, in Malé. Built in 1656, this is the oldest mosque in Maldives. Following the Islamic concept that before Islam there was the time of <a href="/wiki/Jahiliya" class="mw-redirect" title="Jahiliya">Jahiliya</a> (ignorance), in the history books used by Maldivians the <a href="#Introduction_of_Islam">introduction of Islam</a> at the end of the 12th century is considered the cornerstone of the country's history. Nonetheless, the cultural influence of Buddhism remains, a reality directly experienced by Ibn Battuta during his nine months there sometime between 1341 and 1345, serving as a chief judge and marrying into the royal family of <a href="/wiki/Omar_I_of_the_Maldives" title="Omar I of the Maldives">Omar I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> For he became embroiled in local politics and left when his strict judgments in the laissez-faire island kingdom began to chafe with its rulers. In particular, he was dismayed at the local women going about with no clothing above the waist—a violation of Middle Eastern Islamic standards of modesty—and the locals taking no notice when he complained.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Compared to the other areas of South Asia, the conversion of the Maldives to Islam happened relatively late. Arab traders had converted populations in the <a href="/wiki/Malabar_Coast" title="Malabar Coast">Malabar Coast</a> since the 7th century, and <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_bin_Qasim" title="Muhammad bin Qasim">Muhammad Bin Qāsim</a> had converted large swathes of <a href="/wiki/Sindh" title="Sindh">Sindh</a> to Islam at about the same time. The Maldives remained a Buddhist kingdom for another 500 years after the conversion of <a href="/wiki/Malabar_Coast" title="Malabar Coast">Malabar Coast</a> and Sindh—perhaps as the southwesternmost Buddhist country. Arabic became the prime language of administration (instead of Persian and Urdu), and the <a href="/wiki/Maliki" title="Maliki">Maliki</a> school of jurisprudence was introduced, both hinting at direct contacts with the core of the Arab world. </p>
      <p>Middle Eastern seafarers had just begun to take over the Indian Ocean trade routes in the 10th century and found Maldives to be an important link in those routes as the first landfall for traders from <a href="/wiki/Basra" title="Basra">Basra</a> sailing to Southeast Asia. Trade involved mainly <a href="/wiki/Cowrie_shells" class="mw-redirect" title="Cowrie shells">cowrie shells</a>—widely used as a form of currency throughout Asia and parts of the <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East African</a> coast—and coir fiber. The <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Sultanate" title="Bengal Sultanate">Bengal Sultanate</a>, where cowrie shells were used as legal tender, was one of the principal trading partners of the Maldives. The Bengal–Maldives cowry shell trade was the largest shell currency trade network in history.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The other essential product of the Maldives was <a href="/wiki/Coir" title="Coir">coir</a>, the fibre of the dried <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconut</a> <a href="/wiki/Husk" title="Husk">husk</a>, resistant to saltwater. It stitched together and rigged the <a href="/wiki/Dhow" title="Dhow">dhows</a> that plied the Indian Ocean. Maldivian coir was exported to Sindh, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">Colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ConstantinoBraganca.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/ConstantinoBraganca.jpg/220px-ConstantinoBraganca.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/ConstantinoBraganca.jpg/330px-ConstantinoBraganca.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/ConstantinoBraganca.jpg/440px-ConstantinoBraganca.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1497" data-file-height="1584"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ConstantinoBraganca.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese presence</a> in the Maldives was established in 1558, by order of <a href="/wiki/Constantino_of_Braganza" title="Constantino of Braganza">Constantino of Braganza</a>, Viceroy of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Codice_Casanatense_Maldivans.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Codice_Casanatense_Maldivans.jpg/220px-Codice_Casanatense_Maldivans.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Codice_Casanatense_Maldivans.jpg/330px-Codice_Casanatense_Maldivans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Codice_Casanatense_Maldivans.jpg/440px-Codice_Casanatense_Maldivans.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1855" data-file-height="1354"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Codice_Casanatense_Maldivans.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>16th-century Portuguese illustration from the <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3dice_Casanatense" title="Códice Casanatense">Códice Casanatense</a>, depicting workers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:18th-century_Maldives_map_by_Pierre_Mortier.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/18th-century_Maldives_map_by_Pierre_Mortier.jpg/220px-18th-century_Maldives_map_by_Pierre_Mortier.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/18th-century_Maldives_map_by_Pierre_Mortier.jpg/330px-18th-century_Maldives_map_by_Pierre_Mortier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/18th-century_Maldives_map_by_Pierre_Mortier.jpg/440px-18th-century_Maldives_map_by_Pierre_Mortier.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="653"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:18th-century_Maldives_map_by_Pierre_Mortier.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>18th-century map by <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Mortier" class="mw-redirect" title="Pierre Mortier">Pierre Mortier</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, depicting with detail the islands of the Maldives
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1558 the Portuguese established a small garrison with a <i>Viador</i> (<i>Viyazoru</i>), or overseer of a <a href="/wiki/Factory_(trading_post)" title="Factory (trading post)">factory (trading post)</a> in the Maldives, which they administered from their main colony in <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>. Their attempts to impose Christianity provoked a local revolt led by <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Thakurufaanu_Al_Auzam" title="Muhammad Thakurufaanu Al Auzam">Muhammad Thakurufaanu al-A'uẓam</a> and his two brothers, that fifteen years later drove the Portuguese out of Maldives. This event is now commemorated as National Day. </p>
      <p>In the mid-17th century, the Dutch, who had replaced the Portuguese as the dominant power in <a href="/wiki/Ceylon" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceylon">Ceylon</a>, established hegemony over Maldivian affairs without involving themselves directly in local matters, which were governed according to centuries-old Islamic customs. </p>
      <p>The British expelled the Dutch from Ceylon in 1796 and included Maldives as a <a href="/wiki/British_Protectorate" class="mw-redirect" title="British Protectorate">British Protectorate</a>. The status of Maldives as a British protectorate was officially recorded in an 1887 agreement in which the sultan accepted British influence over Maldivian external relations and defence while retaining home rule, which continued to be regulated by <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> traditional institutions in exchange for an <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_annual_tribute" class="mw-redirect" title="Maldivian annual tribute">annual tribute</a>. The status of the islands was akin to other British protectorates in the Indian Ocean region, including <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Trucial_States" title="Trucial States">Trucial States</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maldivas_xvi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Maldivas_xvi.jpg/220px-Maldivas_xvi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Maldivas_xvi.jpg/330px-Maldivas_xvi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Maldivas_xvi.jpg/440px-Maldivas_xvi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maldivas_xvi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>17th century Portuguese drawing of the fortress of Maldives and the archipelago.In Antonio Bocarro book of fortress (1632)<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the British period, the Sultan's powers were taken over by the Chief Minister, much to the chagrin of the British Governor-General who continued to deal with the ineffectual Sultan. Consequently, Britain encouraged the development of a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, and the first Constitution was proclaimed in 1932. However, the new arrangements favoured neither the aging Sultan nor the wily Chief Minister, but rather a young crop of British-educated reformists. As a result, angry mobs were instigated against the Constitution which was publicly torn up. </p>
      <p>Maldives remained a British crown protectorate until 1953 when the sultanate was suspended and the First Republic was declared under the short-lived presidency of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Amin_Didi" class="mw-redirect" title="Muhammad Amin Didi">Muhammad Amin Didi</a>. While serving as prime minister during the 1940s, Didi nationalized the fish export industry. As president, he is remembered as a reformer of the education system and a promoter of <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">women's rights</a>. Conservatives in Malé eventually ousted his government, and during a riot over food shortages, Didi was beaten by a mob and died on a nearby island. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Air_Force_Operations_in_the_Far_East,_1941-1945_CF620.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Royal_Air_Force_Operations_in_the_Far_East%2C_1941-1945_CF620.jpg/220px-Royal_Air_Force_Operations_in_the_Far_East%2C_1941-1945_CF620.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Royal_Air_Force_Operations_in_the_Far_East%2C_1941-1945_CF620.jpg/330px-Royal_Air_Force_Operations_in_the_Far_East%2C_1941-1945_CF620.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Royal_Air_Force_Operations_in_the_Far_East%2C_1941-1945_CF620.jpg/440px-Royal_Air_Force_Operations_in_the_Far_East%2C_1941-1945_CF620.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="544"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Air_Force_Operations_in_the_Far_East,_1941-1945_CF620.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An <a href="/wiki/RAF" class="mw-redirect" title="RAF">RAF</a> <a href="/wiki/Short_Sunderland" title="Short Sunderland">Short Sunderland</a> moored in the lagoon at Addu Atoll, during WWII
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Beginning in the 1950s, the political history in Maldives was largely influenced by the British military presence in the islands. In 1954 the restoration of the sultanate perpetuated the rule of the past. Two years later, the United Kingdom obtained permission to reestablish its wartime <a href="/wiki/RAF_Gan" title="RAF Gan">RAF Gan</a> airfield in the southernmost <a href="/wiki/Addu_Atoll" title="Addu Atoll">Addu Atoll</a>, employing hundreds of locals. In 1957, however, the new prime minister, <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Nasir" title="Ibrahim Nasir">Ibrahim Nasir</a>, called for a review of the agreement. Nasir was challenged in 1959 by a local secessionist movement in the three southernmost atolls that benefited economically from the British presence on <a href="/wiki/Gan_(Seenu_Atoll)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gan (Seenu Atoll)">Gan</a>. This group cut ties with the Maldives government and formed an independent state, the <a href="/wiki/United_Suvadive_Republic" title="United Suvadive Republic">United Suvadive Republic</a> with <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Afif" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdullah Afif">Abdullah Afif</a> as president and <a href="/wiki/Hithadhoo_(Seenu_Atoll)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hithadhoo (Seenu Atoll)">Hithadhoo</a> as capital. One year later the Suvadive republic was scrapped after Nasir sent gunboats from Malé with government police, and Abdulla Afif went into exile. Meanwhile, in 1960 the Maldives had allowed the United Kingdom to continue to use both the <a href="/wiki/RAF_Gan" title="RAF Gan">Gan</a> and the Hitaddu facilities for a thirty-year period, with the payment of £750,000 over the period of 1960 to 1965 for the purpose of Maldives' economic development. The base was closed in 1976 as part of the larger British withdrawal of permanently-stationed forces '<a href="/wiki/East_of_Suez" title="East of Suez">East of Suez</a>'.<sup id="cite_ref-gan.philliptsmall.me.uk_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gan.philliptsmall.me.uk-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_republic">Independence and republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Independence and republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Sultan_of_the_Maldives.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Flag_of_the_Sultan_of_the_Maldives.png/220px-Flag_of_the_Sultan_of_the_Maldives.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Flag_of_the_Sultan_of_the_Maldives.png/330px-Flag_of_the_Sultan_of_the_Maldives.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Flag_of_the_Sultan_of_the_Maldives.png/440px-Flag_of_the_Sultan_of_the_Maldives.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Sultan_of_the_Maldives.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Flag of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Maldives" title="List of sultans of the Maldives">Sultan of the Maldives</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>When the British became increasingly unable to continue their colonial hold on Asia and were losing their colonies to the indigenous populations who wanted freedom, on 26 July 1965 an agreement was signed on behalf of the Sultan by Ibrahim Nasir Rannabandeyri Kilegefan, Prime Minister, and on behalf of the British government by Sir Michael Walker, British Ambassador-designate to the Maldive Islands, which formally ended the British authority on the defence and external affairs of the Maldives. The islands thus achieved freedom, with the ceremony taking place at the British High Commissioner's Residence in <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>. After this, the sultanate continued for another three years under <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Fareed_Didi" title="Muhammad Fareed Didi">Sir Muhammad Fareed Didi</a>, who declared himself King upon independence. </p>
      <p>On 15 November 1967, a vote was taken in parliament to decide whether the Maldives should continue as a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> or become a republic. Of the 44 members of parliament, 40 voted in favour of a republic. On 15 March 1968, a national referendum was held on the question, and 93.34% of those taking part voted in favour of establishing a republic. The republic was declared on 11 November 1968, thus ending the 853-year-old monarchy, which was replaced by a republic under the presidency of <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Nasir" title="Ibrahim Nasir">Ibrahim Nasir</a>. As the King had held little real power, this was seen as a cosmetic change and required few alterations in the structures of government. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_the_Maldives" title="Tourism in the Maldives">Tourism</a> began to be developed on the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> by the beginning of the 1970s. The first resort in the Maldives was <a href="/wiki/Kurumba_Maldives" title="Kurumba Maldives">Kurumba Maldives</a> which welcomed the first guests on 3 October 1972. The first accurate census was held in December 1977 and showed 142,832 people living in the Maldives.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Political infighting during the 1970s between Nasir's faction and other political figures led to the 1975 arrest and exile of elected prime minister <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Zaki_(politician)" title="Ahmed Zaki (politician)">Ahmed Zaki</a> to a remote <a href="/wiki/Atoll" title="Atoll">atoll</a>. Economic decline followed the closure of the <a href="/wiki/Gan_International_Airport" title="Gan International Airport">British airfield at Gan</a> and the collapse of the market for dried fish, an important export. With support for his administration faltering, Nasir fled to Singapore in 1978, with millions of dollars from the treasury. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Maumoon_Abdul_Gayoom" title="Maumoon Abdul Gayoom">Maumoon Abdul Gayoom</a> began his 30-year role as president in 1978, winning six consecutive elections without opposition. His election was seen as ushering in a period of political stability and economic development in view of Maumoon's priority to develop the poorer islands. Tourism flourished and increased foreign contact spurred development. However, Maumoon's rule was controversial, with some critics saying Maumoon was an autocrat who quelled dissent by limiting freedoms and political favouritism.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_sinking_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_sinking-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A series of coup attempts (in 1980, 1983, and 1988) by Nasir supporters and business interests tried to topple the government without success. While the first two attempts met with little success, the 1988 coup attempt involved a roughly 80 strong mercenary force of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Organisation_of_Tamil_Eelam" title="People's Liberation Organisation of Tamil Eelam">PLOTE</a> who seized the airport and caused Maumoon to flee from house to house until the intervention of 1,600 <a href="/wiki/Indian_Armed_Forces" title="Indian Armed Forces">Indian troops</a> airlifted into <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9" title="Malé">Malé</a> restored order. </p>
      <p>The November 1988 coup was headed by Muhammadu Ibrahim Lutfee, a businessman. On the night of 3 November 1988, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">Indian Air Force</a> airlifted a <a href="/wiki/Parachute_Regiment_(India)#Operation_Cactus" title="Parachute Regiment (India)">parachute battalion group</a> from <a href="/wiki/Agra" title="Agra">Agra</a> and flew them over 2,000 kilometres (1,200&nbsp;mi) to the Maldives. The Indian <a href="/wiki/Paratroopers" class="mw-redirect" title="Paratroopers">paratroopers</a> landed at <a href="/wiki/Hulhul%C3%A9_Island" title="Hulhulé Island">Hulhulé</a> and secured the airfield and restored the government rule at Malé within hours. The brief operation, labelled <i><a href="/wiki/Operation_Cactus" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Cactus">Operation Cactus</a></i>, also involved the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Navy" title="Indian Navy">Indian Navy</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twenty-first_century">Twenty-first century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Twenty-first century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Maldives#21st_century" title="History of the Maldives">History of the Maldives §&nbsp;21st century</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Prime_Minister,_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_along_with_other_Head_of_State_and_Government_of_SAARC_Countries,_at_the_inaugural_session_of_the_17th_SAARC_Summit,_at_Adu_Atoll_in_Maldives_on_November_10,_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_along_with_other_Head_of_State_and_Government_of_SAARC_Countries%2C_at_the_inaugural_session_of_the_17th_SAARC_Summit%2C_at_Adu_Atoll_in_Maldives_on_November_10%2C_2011.jpg/250px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_along_with_other_Head_of_State_and_Government_of_SAARC_Countries%2C_at_the_inaugural_session_of_the_17th_SAARC_Summit%2C_at_Adu_Atoll_in_Maldives_on_November_10%2C_2011.jpg/375px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_along_with_other_Head_of_State_and_Government_of_SAARC_Countries%2C_at_the_inaugural_session_of_the_17th_SAARC_Summit%2C_at_Adu_Atoll_in_Maldives_on_November_10%2C_2011.jpg/500px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="912"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Prime_Minister,_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_along_with_other_Head_of_State_and_Government_of_SAARC_Countries,_at_the_inaugural_session_of_the_17th_SAARC_Summit,_at_Adu_Atoll_in_Maldives_on_November_10,_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/17th_SAARC_summit" title="17th SAARC summit">17th SAARC summit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Addu_City" title="Addu City">Addu City</a>, Maldives
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 26 December 2004, following the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake">2004 Indian Ocean earthquake</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_the_2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_on_the_Maldives" title="Effect of the 2004 Indian Ocean earthquake on the Maldives">Maldives were devastated</a> by a tsunami. Only nine islands were reported to have escaped any flooding,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> while fifty-seven islands faced serious damage to critical infrastructure, fourteen islands had to be totally evacuated, and six islands were destroyed. A further twenty-one resort islands were forced to close because of tsunami damage. The total damage was estimated at more than US$400&nbsp;million, or some 62% of the GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> 102 Maldivians and 6 foreigners reportedly died in the tsunami.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_sinking_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_sinking-58">[58]</a></sup> The destructive impact of the waves on the low-lying islands was mitigated by the fact there was no continental shelf or land mass upon which the waves could gain height. The tallest waves were reported to be 14 feet (4.3&nbsp;m) high.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the later part of Maumoon's rule, independent political movements emerged in Maldives, which challenged the then-ruling <a href="/wiki/Dhivehi_Rayyithunge_Party" title="Dhivehi Rayyithunge Party">Dhivehi Rayyithunge Party</a> (Maldivian People's Party, MPP) and demanded democratic reform. The dissident journalist and activist <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Nasheed" title="Mohamed Nasheed">Mohamed Nasheed</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_Democratic_Party" title="Maldivian Democratic Party">Maldivian Democratic Party</a> (MDP) in 2003 and pressured Maumoon into allowing gradual political reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-brownpoliticalreview.org_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brownpoliticalreview.org-64">[64]</a></sup> In 2008 a new constitution was approved and the <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_presidential_election,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Maldivian presidential election, 2008">first direct presidential elections</a> occurred, which were won by Nasheed in the second round. His administration faced many challenges, including the huge debt left by the previous government, the economic downturn following the 2004 tsunami, overspending by means of overprinting of local currency (the <a href="/wiki/Rufiyaa" class="mw-redirect" title="Rufiyaa">rufiyaa</a>), unemployment, corruption, and increasing drug use.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (April 2013)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> Taxation on goods was imposed for the first time in the country, and import duties were reduced in many goods and services. Social welfare benefits were given to those aged 65 years or older, single parents, and those with special needs.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_sinking_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_sinking-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Social and <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Maldives_political_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2011–12 Maldives political crisis">political unrest grew in late 2011</a>, following opposition campaigns in the name of protecting <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. Nasheed controversially resigned from office after large number of police and army mutinied in February 2012. Nasheed's vice president, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Waheed_Hassan" title="Mohammed Waheed Hassan">Mohammed Waheed Hassan</a>, was sworn in as president.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Nasheed was later arrested,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> convicted of terrorism, and sentenced to 13 years. The trial was widely seen as flawed and political. The UN Working Group on Arbitrary Detention called for Nasheed's immediate release.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_presidential_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Maldivian presidential election, 2013">elections in late 2013</a> were highly contested. Former president Nasheed won the most votes in the first round, but the Supreme Court annulled it despite the positive assessment of international election observers. In the re-run vote <a href="/wiki/Abdulla_Yameen" title="Abdulla Yameen">Abdulla Yameen</a>, half-brother of the former president Maumoon, assumed the presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-brownpoliticalreview.org_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brownpoliticalreview.org-64">[64]</a></sup> Yameen introduced increased engagement with China, and promoted a policy of connecting Islam with anti-Western rhetoric.<sup id="cite_ref-brownpoliticalreview.org_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brownpoliticalreview.org-64">[64]</a></sup> Yameen survived an assassination attempt in late 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Vice president <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Adeeb" title="Ahmed Adeeb">Ahmed Adeeb</a> was later arrested together with 17 supporters for "public order offences" and the government instituted a broader crackdown against political dissent. A <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> was later declared ahead of a planned anti-government rally,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Majlis" title="People's Majlis">people's Majlis</a> accelerated the removal of Adeeb.<sup id="cite_ref-majlis.gov.mv_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-majlis.gov.mv-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2018 elections <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Mohamed_Solih" title="Ibrahim Mohamed Solih">Ibrahim Mohamed Solih</a> won the most votes, and became President. </p>
      <p>Adeeb was freed by courts in Male in July 2019 after his conviction on charges of terrorism and corruption was overruled, but was placed under a travel ban after the state prosecutor appealed the order in a corruption and money laundering case. Adeeb escaped in a tugboat to seek asylum in India. It is understood that the Indian Coast Guard escorted the tugboat to the International Maritime Boundary Line (IMBL) and he was then “transferred” to a Maldivian Coast Guard ship, where officials took him into custody.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Maldives" title="Geography of the Maldives">Geography of the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Malosmadulu_Atolls,_Maldives.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Malosmadulu_Atolls%2C_Maldives.jpg/170px-Malosmadulu_Atolls%2C_Maldives.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Malosmadulu_Atolls%2C_Maldives.jpg/255px-Malosmadulu_Atolls%2C_Maldives.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Malosmadulu_Atolls%2C_Maldives.jpg/340px-Malosmadulu_Atolls%2C_Maldives.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1687" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Malosmadulu_Atolls,_Maldives.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Maalhosmadulu Atoll seen from space. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Maalhosmadulu_Atoll" title="Northern Maalhosmadulu Atoll">Northern Maalhosmadulu Atoll</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Maalhosmadulu_Atoll" title="Southern Maalhosmadulu Atoll">Southern Maalhosmadulu Atoll</a> can be seen in this picture.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Man_on_sand_bank_in_the_Maldives_looking_at_sea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Man_on_sand_bank_in_the_Maldives_looking_at_sea.jpg/220px-Man_on_sand_bank_in_the_Maldives_looking_at_sea.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Man_on_sand_bank_in_the_Maldives_looking_at_sea.jpg/330px-Man_on_sand_bank_in_the_Maldives_looking_at_sea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Man_on_sand_bank_in_the_Maldives_looking_at_sea.jpg/440px-Man_on_sand_bank_in_the_Maldives_looking_at_sea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2880"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Man_on_sand_bank_in_the_Maldives_looking_at_sea.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dark clouds as a pretext for heavy rains, common in the rainy season.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Maldives consists of 1,192 <a href="/wiki/Coral_island" title="Coral island">coral islands</a> grouped in a double chain of 26 <a href="/wiki/Atoll" title="Atoll">atolls</a>, that stretch along a length of 871 kilometres (541 miles) north to south, 130 kilometres (81 miles) east to west, spread over roughly 90,000 square kilometres (35,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), of which only 298&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (115&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) is dry land, making this one of the world's most dispersed countries. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/1st_parallel_south" title="1st parallel south">1°S</a> and <a href="/wiki/8th_parallel_north" title="8th parallel north">8°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/72nd_meridian_east" title="72nd meridian east">72°</a> and <a href="/wiki/74th_meridian_east" title="74th meridian east">74°E</a>. The atolls are composed of live <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sand_bar" class="mw-redirect" title="Sand bar">sand bars</a>, situated atop a submarine ridge 960 kilometres (600&nbsp;mi) long that rises abruptly from the depths of the Indian Ocean and runs north to south. </p>
      <p>Only near the southern end of this natural coral barricade do two open passages permit safe ship navigation from one side of the Indian Ocean to the other through the territorial waters of Maldives. For administrative purposes, the Maldivian government organised these atolls into 21 <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Maldives" title="Administrative divisions of the Maldives">administrative divisions</a>. The largest island of Maldives is that of <a href="/wiki/Gan_(Laamu_Atoll)" title="Gan (Laamu Atoll)">Gan</a>, which belongs to Laamu Atoll or Hahdhummathi Maldives. In <a href="/wiki/Addu_Atoll" title="Addu Atoll">Addu Atoll</a>, the westernmost islands are connected by roads over the reef (collectively called Link Road) and the total length of the road is 14&nbsp;km (9&nbsp;mi). </p>
      <p>Maldives is the lowest country in the world, with maximum and average natural ground levels of only 2.4 metres (7&nbsp;ft 10&nbsp;in) and 1.5 metres (4&nbsp;ft 11&nbsp;in) above sea level, respectively. In areas where construction exists, however, this has been increased to several metres. More than 80 per cent of the country's land is composed of coral islands which rise less than one metre above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> As a result, the Maldives are at high risk of being submerged due to <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">rising sea levels</a>. The <a href="/wiki/IPCC" class="mw-redirect" title="IPCC">UN's environmental panel</a> has warned that, at current rates, sea-level rise would be high enough to make the Maldives uninhabitable by 2100.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bathala_(Maldives)_8.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Bathala_%28Maldives%29_8.JPG/220px-Bathala_%28Maldives%29_8.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Bathala_%28Maldives%29_8.JPG/330px-Bathala_%28Maldives%29_8.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Bathala_%28Maldives%29_8.JPG/440px-Bathala_%28Maldives%29_8.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bathala_(Maldives)_8.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A beach of <a href="/wiki/Bathala_(island)" title="Bathala (island)">Bathala</a> island
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Maldives has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon climate</a> (Am) under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, which is affected by the large landmass of South Asia to the north. Because the Maldives has the lowest elevation of any country in the world, the temperature is constantly hot and often humid. The presence of this landmass causes differential heating of land and water. These factors set off a rush of moisture-rich air from the Indian Ocean over South Asia, resulting in the southwest <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>. Two seasons dominate Maldives' weather: the dry season associated with the winter northeastern monsoon and the rainy season associated with the southwest monsoon which brings strong winds and storms. </p>
      <p>The shift from the dry northeast monsoon to the moist southwest monsoon occurs during April and May. During this period, the southwest winds contribute to the formation of the southwest monsoon, which reaches Maldives at the beginning of June and lasts until the end of November. However, the weather patterns of Maldives do not always conform to the monsoon patterns of South Asia. The annual rainfall averages 254 centimetres (100&nbsp;in) in the north and 381 centimetres (150&nbsp;in) in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The monsoonal influence is greater in the north of the Maldives than in the south, more influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Counter_Current" title="Equatorial Counter Current">equatorial currents</a>. </p>
      <p>The average high temperature is 31.5 degree Celsius and the average low temperature is 26.4 degree Celsius. </p>
