      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea_level_rise">Sea level rise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sea level rise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Island_President" title="The Island President">The Island President</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a>'s 2007 report predicted the upper limit of the <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rises</a> will be 59 centimetres (23&nbsp;in) by 2100, which means that most of the republic's 200 inhabited islands may need to be abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> According to researchers from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southampton" title="University of Southampton">University of Southampton</a>, the Maldives are the third most endangered island nation due to flooding from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> as a percentage of population.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Former president <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Nasheed" title="Mohamed Nasheed">Mohamed Nasheed</a> has been highly outspoken about this issue, saying in 2012 that "If carbon emissions continue at the rate they are climbing today, my country will be under water in seven years."<sup id="cite_ref-Guilfordian_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guilfordian-82">[82]</a></sup> He has called for more <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">climate change mitigation</a> action while on the American television shows <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">The Daily Show</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Guilfordian_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guilfordian-82">[82]</a></sup> and hosted "the world's first underwater cabinet meeting" in 2009 to raise awareness of the threats posed by climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Concerns over sea level rise have also been expressed by Nasheed's predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Maumoon_Abdul_Gayoom" title="Maumoon Abdul Gayoom">Maumoon Abdul Gayoom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008, Nasheed announced plans to look into purchasing new land in India, Sri Lanka, and Australia because of his concerns about global warming, and the possibility of much of the islands being inundated with water from rising sea levels. The purchase of land will be made from a fund generated by tourism. The president explained his intentions: "We do not want to leave the Maldives, but we also do not want to be <a href="/wiki/Climate_refugee" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate refugee">climate refugees</a> living in tents for decades".<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> By 2020,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (March 2020)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> Maldives plans to eliminate or offset all of its greenhouse gas emissions. At the 2009 International Climate Talks, Nasheed explained that: </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>For us swearing off fossil fuels is not only the right thing to do, it is in our economic self-interest... Pioneering countries will free themselves from the unpredictable price of foreign oil; they will capitalise on the new green economy of the future, and they will enhance their moral standing giving them greater political influence on the world stage.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>In 2020, a three-year study at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Plymouth" title="University of Plymouth">University of Plymouth</a> found that as tides move sediment to create higher elevation, the islands, and also <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>, may rise instead of sink.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment<span class="anchor" id="Environmental_issues"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Environmental issues other than <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a> include bad waste disposal and <a href="/wiki/Beach_theft" class="mw-redirect" title="Beach theft">beach theft</a>. Although the Maldives are kept relatively pristine and little <a href="/wiki/Litter" title="Litter">litter</a> can be found on the islands, no good <a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">waste disposal</a> sites exist. Most trash from Malé and other resorts is simply dumped at <a href="/wiki/Thilafushi" title="Thilafushi">Thilafushi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Protected_Areas_of_Maldives" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Protected Areas of Maldives">31 protected areas</a> are administered by the Ministry of Environment and Energy and Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) of the Maldives.<sup id="cite_ref-Maldives_Protected_Areas_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maldives_Protected_Areas-91">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_ecosystem">Marine ecosystem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Marine ecosystem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Maldives" title="Wildlife of Maldives">Wildlife of Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maldives_soft_coral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Maldives_soft_coral.jpg/220px-Maldives_soft_coral.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Maldives_soft_coral.jpg/330px-Maldives_soft_coral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Maldives_soft_coral.jpg/440px-Maldives_soft_coral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maldives_soft_coral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Maldives soft coral
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maldives_Oriental_sweetlips,_Plectorhinchus_vittatus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Maldives_Oriental_sweetlips%2C_Plectorhinchus_vittatus.jpg/170px-Maldives_Oriental_sweetlips%2C_Plectorhinchus_vittatus.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Maldives_Oriental_sweetlips%2C_Plectorhinchus_vittatus.jpg/255px-Maldives_Oriental_sweetlips%2C_Plectorhinchus_vittatus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Maldives_Oriental_sweetlips%2C_Plectorhinchus_vittatus.jpg/340px-Maldives_Oriental_sweetlips%2C_Plectorhinchus_vittatus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maldives_Oriental_sweetlips,_Plectorhinchus_vittatus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Oriental_sweetlips" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental sweetlips">Oriental sweetlips</a> (<i>Plectorhinchus vittatus</i>) at <a href="/wiki/Meeru_Island" title="Meeru Island">Meeru Island</a>, North Male Atoll
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Maldives have a range of different habitats including deep sea, shallow coast, and reef ecosystems, fringing mangroves, wetlands and dry land. There are 187 species of coral forming the <a href="/wiki/Coral_reefs" class="mw-redirect" title="Coral reefs">coral reefs</a>. This area of the Indian Ocean, alone, houses 1,100 <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> of fish, 5 species of <a href="/wiki/Sea_turtle" title="Sea turtle">sea turtle</a>, 21 species of whale and dolphin, 400 species of mollusc, and 83 species of echinoderms. The area is also populated by a number of crustacean species: 120 copepods, 15 amphipods, as well as more than 145 crab and 48 shrimp species.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Among the many marine families represented are <a href="/wiki/Pufferfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Pufferfish">pufferfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caesionidae" title="Caesionidae">fusiliers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carangidae" title="Carangidae">jackfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lionfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Lionfish">lionfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oriental_sweetlips" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental sweetlips">oriental sweetlips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reef_sharks" class="mw-redirect" title="Reef sharks">reef sharks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grouper" title="Grouper">groupers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eel" title="Eel">eels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutjanidae" title="Lutjanidae">snappers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bannerfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Bannerfish">bannerfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ogcocephalidae" title="Ogcocephalidae">batfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humphead_wrasse" title="Humphead wrasse">humphead wrasse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spotted_eagle_ray" title="Spotted eagle ray">spotted eagle rays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scorpionfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Scorpionfish">scorpionfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobster" title="Lobster">lobsters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nudibranches" class="mw-redirect" title="Nudibranches">nudibranches</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pomacanthidae" title="Pomacanthidae">angelfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Butterflyfish" title="Butterflyfish">butterflyfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squirrelfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Squirrelfish">squirrelfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soldierfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Soldierfish">soldierfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_glassfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Asiatic glassfish">glassfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surgeonfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Surgeonfish">surgeonfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naso_(fish)" title="Naso (fish)">unicornfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Triggerfish" title="Triggerfish">triggerfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_wrasse" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon wrasse">Napoleon wrasse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barracuda" title="Barracuda">barracuda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-scuba_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scuba-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>These coral reefs are home to a variety of marine ecosystems that vary from <a href="/wiki/Planktonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Planktonic">planktonic</a> organisms to whale sharks. Sponges have gained importance as five species have displayed anti-tumor and anti-cancer properties.<sup id="cite_ref-Coral_reefs_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coral_reefs-95">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1998, sea-temperature warming of as much as 5&nbsp;°C (9.0&nbsp;°F) due to a single <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" class="mw-redirect" title="El Niño-Southern Oscillation">El Niño phenomenon</a> event caused <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">coral bleaching</a>, killing two-thirds of the nation's coral reefs.<sup id="cite_ref-Wheatley_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wheatley-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In an effort to induce the regrowth of the reefs, scientists placed electrified cones anywhere from 20–60 feet (6.1–18.3&nbsp;m) below the surface to provide a substrate for larval coral attachment. In 2004, scientists witnessed corals regenerating. Corals began to eject pink-orange eggs and sperm. The growth of these electrified corals was five times faster than untreated corals.<sup id="cite_ref-Wheatley_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wheatley-96">[96]</a></sup> Scientist Azeez Hakim stated: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>before 1998, we never thought that this reef would die. We had always taken for granted that these animals would be there, that this reef would be there forever. El Niño gave us a wake-up call that these things are not going to be there forever. Not only this, they also act as a natural barrier against the tropical storms, floods and tsunamis. Seaweeds grow on the skeletons of dead coral.</p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        — <cite><sup id="cite_ref-scuba_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scuba-93">[93]</a></sup></cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>Again, in 2016, the coral reefs of the Maldives experienced a <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching#Maldives" title="Coral bleaching">severe bleaching incident</a>. Up to 95% of coral around some islands have died, and, even after six months, 100% of young coral transplants died. The surface water temperatures reached an all-time high in 2016, at 31 degrees Celsius in May.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Recent scientific studies suggest that the faunistic composition can vary greatly between neighbour atolls, especially in terms of benthic fauna. Differences in terms of fishing pressure (including poaching) could be the cause.<sup id="cite_ref-Ducarme_between_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ducarme_between-98">[98]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Maldives" title="Politics of the Maldives">Politics of the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:JumhooreeMaidan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/JumhooreeMaidan.JPG/220px-JumhooreeMaidan.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/JumhooreeMaidan.JPG/330px-JumhooreeMaidan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/JumhooreeMaidan.JPG/440px-JumhooreeMaidan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:JumhooreeMaidan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Republic Square in Malé
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Maldives is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> republic, with extensive influence of the president as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. The president heads the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive branch</a>, and appoints the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_Maldives" title="Cabinet of the Maldives">cabinet</a> which is approved by the <a href="/wiki/Majlis_of_the_Maldives" class="mw-redirect" title="Majlis of the Maldives">People's Majlis (Parliament)</a>. He leads the <a href="/wiki/Maldives_National_Defence_Force" title="Maldives National Defence Force">armed forces</a>. There is no separation of powers. The current president as of 17 November 2018 is <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Mohamed_Solih" title="Ibrahim Mohamed Solih">Ibrahim Mohamed Solih</a>. Members of the <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> Majlis serve five-year terms, with the total number of members determined by atoll populations. At the <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_parliamentary_election,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Maldivian parliamentary election, 2014">2014 election</a>, 77 members were elected. The People's Majlis, located in <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9" title="Malé">Malé</a>, houses members from all over the country.<sup id="cite_ref-r1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The republican constitution came into force in 1968, and was amended in 1970, 1972, and 1975. On 27 November 1997 it was replaced by another Constitution assented to by then-President <a href="/wiki/Maumoon_Abdul_Gayoom" title="Maumoon Abdul Gayoom">Maumoon</a>. This Constitution came into force on 1 January 1998. The current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Maldives" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of Maldives">Constitution of Maldives</a> was ratified by President Maumoon on 7 August 2008, and came into effect immediately, replacing and repealing the constitution of 1998. This new constitution includes a judiciary run by an independent commission, and independent commissions to oversee elections and fight corruption. It also reduces the executive powers vested under the president and strengthens the parliament. All state that the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Maldives" title="President of the Maldives">president</a> is head of state, head of government and Commander-in-Chief of the <a href="/wiki/Maldives_National_Defence_Force" title="Maldives National Defence Force">armed forces</a> of the Maldives. </p>
      <p>In 2018, the ruling <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Party_of_Maldives" title="Progressive Party of Maldives">Progressive Party of Maldives</a> (PPM-Y)'s tensions with opposition parties and subsequent crackdown was termed as an "assault on democracy" by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">UN Human Rights</a> chief.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Prime_Minister,_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_addressing_at_the_People%E2%80%99s_Majlis,_at_Male,_in_Maldives_on_November_12,_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_addressing_at_the_People%E2%80%99s_Majlis%2C_at_Male%2C_in_Maldives_on_November_12%2C_2011.jpg/220px-The_Prime_Minister%2C_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_addressing_at_the_People%E2%80%99s_Majlis%2C_at_Male%2C_in_Maldives_on_November_12%2C_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_addressing_at_the_People%E2%80%99s_Majlis%2C_at_Male%2C_in_Maldives_on_November_12%2C_2011.jpg/330px-The_Prime_Minister%2C_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_addressing_at_the_People%E2%80%99s_Majlis%2C_at_Male%2C_in_Maldives_on_November_12%2C_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_addressing_at_the_People%E2%80%99s_Majlis%2C_at_Male%2C_in_Maldives_on_November_12%2C_2011.jpg/440px-The_Prime_Minister%2C_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_addressing_at_the_People%E2%80%99s_Majlis%2C_at_Male%2C_in_Maldives_on_November_12%2C_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1848" data-file-height="2784"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Prime_Minister,_Dr._Manmohan_Singh_addressing_at_the_People%E2%80%99s_Majlis,_at_Male,_in_Maldives_on_November_12,_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Prime Minister of India addressing the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Majlis" title="People's Majlis">People's Majlis</a> in 2011
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_in_the_Maldives" class="mw-redirect" title="Judiciary in the Maldives">Judiciary in the Maldives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_the_Maldives" title="Law enforcement in the Maldives">Law enforcement in the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Maldives" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of Maldives">Constitution of Maldives</a>, "the judges are independent, and subject only to the Constitution and the law. When deciding matters on which the Constitution or the law is silent, judges must consider Islamic <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Shari'ah</a>". </p>
      <p>Islam is the official religion of the Maldives and open practice of any other religion is forbidden.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The 2008 constitution says that the republic "is based on the principles of Islam" and that "no law contrary to any principle of Islam can be applied". Non-Muslims are prohibited from becoming citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-Hirschl2011_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hirschl2011-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The requirement to adhere to a particular religion and prohibition of public worship following other religions is contrary to Article 18 of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> and Article 18 of the <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Civil_and_Political_Rights" title="International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights">International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights</a> to which Maldives has recently become party<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and was addressed in Maldives' reservation in adhering to the Covenant claiming that "The application of the principles set out in Article 18 of the Covenant shall be without prejudice to the Constitution of the Republic of the Maldives."<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A new <a href="/wiki/Criminal_code" title="Criminal code">penal code</a> came into effect on July 16, 2015, replacing the 1968 law, the first modern, comprehensive penal code to incorporate the major tenets and principles of Islamic law.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">Same-sex relations</a> are illegal in the Maldives, although tourist resorts typically operate as exceptions to this law.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Maldives" title="Foreign relations of the Maldives">Foreign relations of the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Maldives_Foreign_Minister_Shahid_in_Washington_(32217203777).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Maldives_Foreign_Minister_Shahid_in_Washington_%2832217203777%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Maldives_Foreign_Minister_Shahid_in_Washington_%2832217203777%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Maldives_Foreign_Minister_Shahid_in_Washington_%2832217203777%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Maldives_Foreign_Minister_Shahid_in_Washington_%2832217203777%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Maldives_Foreign_Minister_Shahid_in_Washington_%2832217203777%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Maldives_Foreign_Minister_Shahid_in_Washington_%2832217203777%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1932" data-file-height="1287"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Maldives_Foreign_Minister_Shahid_in_Washington_(32217203777).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>US Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a> hosts Maldivian foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Abdulla_Shahid" title="Abdulla Shahid">Abdulla Shahid</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 1996, the Maldives has been the official progress monitor of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Commission" title="Indian Ocean Commission">Indian Ocean Commission</a>. In 2002, the Maldives began to express interest in the commission but as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> had not applied for membership. Maldives' interest relates to its identity as a small island state, especially economic development and environmental preservation, and its desire for closer relations with France, a main actor in the IOC region. </p>
      <p>The Maldives is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation</a> (<a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">SAARC</a>). The republic joined the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> in 1982, some 17 years after gaining independence from the United Kingdom. In October 2016, Maldives announced its withdrawal from the Commonwealth<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> in protest at allegations of human rights abuse and failing democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The Maldives enjoys close ties with Commonwealth members <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>. The Maldives and <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a> are also both members of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>. Following his election as president in 2018, <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Mohamed_Solih" title="Ibrahim Mohamed Solih">Ibrahim Mohamed Solih</a> and his Cabinet decided that the Maldives would apply to rejoin the Commonwealth,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> with readmission occurring on 1 February 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maldives_National_Defence_Force" title="Maldives National Defence Force">Maldives National Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maldives-vaixells_de_bombers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Maldives-vaixells_de_bombers.jpg/220px-Maldives-vaixells_de_bombers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Maldives-vaixells_de_bombers.jpg/330px-Maldives-vaixells_de_bombers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Maldives-vaixells_de_bombers.jpg/440px-Maldives-vaixells_de_bombers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1119" data-file-height="645"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maldives-vaixells_de_bombers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fire &amp; Rescue Service boats
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Maldives National Defence Force is the combined security organisation responsible for defending the security and sovereignty of the Maldives, having the primary task of being responsible for attending to all internal and external security needs of the Maldives, including the protection of the Exclusive Economic Zone (EEZ) and the maintenance of peace and security. The MNDF component branches are the Coast Guard, Marine Corps, Special Forces, Service Corps, and the Corps of Engineers. </p>
      <p>As a water-bound nation, much of its security concerns lie at sea. Almost 99% of the country is covered by sea and the remaining 1% land is scattered over an area of 800&nbsp;km (497&nbsp;mi) × 120&nbsp;km (75&nbsp;mi), with the largest island being not more than 8&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (3&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). Therefore, the duties assigned to the MNDF of maintaining surveillance over Maldives' waters and providing protection against foreign intruders poaching in the EEZ and territorial waters, are immense tasks from both logistical and economic viewpoints. In 2019, Maldives signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Coast Guard plays a vital role in carrying out these functions. To provide timely security its patrol boats are stationed at various MNDF Regional Headquarters. The Coast Guard is also assigned to respond to the maritime distress calls and to conduct search and rescue operations in a timely manner. Maritime pollution control exercises are conducted regularly on an annual basis for familiarisation and handling of such hazardous situations. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Maldives" title="Human rights in the Maldives">Human rights in the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Human rights in the Maldives is a contentious issue. In its 2011 <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a> report, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> declared the Maldives "Partly Free", claiming a reform process which had made headway in 2009 and 2010 had stalled.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_2011_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH_2011-114">[114]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Democracy,_Human_Rights_and_Labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Bureau of Democracy, Human Rights and Labor">United States Bureau of Democracy, Human Rights and Labor</a> claims in their 2012 report on human rights practices in the country that the most significant problems are corruption, lack of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">religious freedom</a>, and abuse and unequal treatment of women.<sup id="cite_ref-State_2012_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_2012-115">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Maldives" title="Administrative divisions of the Maldives">Administrative divisions of the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Atolls_of_the_maldives.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Atolls_of_the_maldives.png/220px-Atolls_of_the_maldives.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="409" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Atolls_of_the_maldives.png/330px-Atolls_of_the_maldives.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Atolls_of_the_maldives.png/440px-Atolls_of_the_maldives.png 2x" data-file-width="618" data-file-height="1149"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Atolls_of_the_maldives.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Each administrative atoll is marked, along with the <a href="/wiki/Thaana" title="Thaana">thaana</a> letter used to identify the atoll. Natural atolls are labelled in light blue. <a class="external text" href="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/Atolls_of_the_maldives.png">Full view of the map</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Maldives has twenty-six natural <a href="/wiki/Atolls_of_the_Maldives" title="Atolls of the Maldives">atolls</a> and few island groups on isolated reefs, all of which have been divided into twenty-one administrative divisions (17 administrative atolls and cities of <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9" title="Malé">Malé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Addu_City" title="Addu City">Addu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuvahmulah" title="Fuvahmulah">Fuvahmulah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kulhudhuffushi" title="Kulhudhuffushi">Kulhudhuffushi</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Each atoll is administered by an elected Atoll Council. The islands are administered by an elected Island Council. </p>
      <p>In addition to a name, every administrative division is identified by the Maldivian code letters, such as "<a href="/wiki/Haa_Alif" class="mw-redirect" title="Haa Alif">Haa Alif</a>" for <a href="/wiki/Northern_Thiladhunmathi_Atoll" title="Northern Thiladhunmathi Atoll">Thiladhunmati Uthuruburi</a> (Thiladhunmathi North); and by a Latin code letter. The first corresponds to the geographical Maldivian name of the atoll; the second is a code adopted for convenience. As there are certain islands in different atolls that have the same name, for administrative purposes this code is quoted before the name of the island, for example: Baa Funadhoo, Kaafu Funadhoo, Gaafu-Alifu Funadhoo. Since most atolls have very long geographical names it is also used whenever the long name is inconvenient, for example in the atoll website names.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The introduction of code-letter names has been a source of much puzzlement and misunderstandings, especially among foreigners. Many people have come to think that the code-letter of the administrative atoll is its new name and that it has replaced its geographical name. Under such circumstances it is hard to know which is the correct name to use.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Maldives" title="Economy of the Maldives">Economy of the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

         <td class="mbox-image">

          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">

      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_western_side_(382669110).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_western_side_%28382669110%29.jpg/220px-The_western_side_%28382669110%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_western_side_%28382669110%29.jpg/330px-The_western_side_%28382669110%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_western_side_%28382669110%29.jpg/440px-The_western_side_%28382669110%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_western_side_(382669110).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Malé harbour
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maldives_treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Maldives_treemap.png/220px-Maldives_treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Maldives_treemap.png/330px-Maldives_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Maldives_treemap.png/440px-Maldives_treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="1106" data-file-height="864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maldives_treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Maldives's product exports in 28 color-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Historically, the Maldives provided enormous quantities of <a href="/wiki/Cowry" class="mw-redirect" title="Cowry">cowry</a> shells, <a href="/wiki/History_of_money" title="History of money">an international currency of the early ages</a>. From the 2nd century AD, the islands were known as the 'Money Isles' by the Arabs.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Monetaria_moneta" title="Monetaria moneta">Monetaria moneta</a></i> were used for centuries as a currency in Africa, and huge amounts of <a href="/wiki/Maldive_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Maldive Islands">Maldivian</a> cowries were introduced into Africa by western nations during the period of <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The cowry is now the symbol of the <a href="/wiki/Maldives_Monetary_Authority" title="Maldives Monetary Authority">Maldives Monetary Authority</a>. </p>
      <p>In the early 1970s, the Maldives was one of the world's 20 poorest countries, with a population of 100,000. The economy at the time was largely dependent on fisheries and trading local goods such as <a href="/wiki/Coir" title="Coir">coir</a> rope, <a href="/wiki/Ambergris" title="Ambergris">ambergris</a> (Maavaharu), and <a href="/wiki/Coco_de_mer" class="mw-redirect" title="Coco de mer">coco de mer</a> (Tavakkaashi) with neighboring countries and <a href="/wiki/East_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="East Asian">East Asian</a> countries. </p>
      <p>The Maldivian government began a largely successful <a href="/wiki/Economic_reform" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic reform">economic reform</a> programme in the 1980s, initiated by lifting import quotas and giving more opportunities to the private sector. At the time <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> sector which would play a significant role in the nation's development was at its infant stage. </p>
      <p>Agriculture and manufacturing continue to play lesser roles in the economy, constrained by the limited availability of cultivable land and the shortage of domestic labour. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_the_Maldives" title="Tourism in the Maldives">Tourism in the Maldives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diving_in_the_Maldives" title="Diving in the Maldives">Diving in the Maldives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mosques_in_the_Maldives" title="List of mosques in the Maldives">List of mosques in the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Filitheyo_bar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Filitheyo_bar.jpg/220px-Filitheyo_bar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Filitheyo_bar.jpg/330px-Filitheyo_bar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Filitheyo_bar.jpg/440px-Filitheyo_bar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Filitheyo_bar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Filitheyo island beach with tall palm trees and blue fresh lagoons
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Maldives remained largely unknown to tourists until the early 1970s. Only 189 islands are home to its 447,137 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The other islands are used entirely for economic purposes, of which tourism and agriculture are the most dominant. Tourism accounts for 28% of the GDP and more than 60% of the Maldives' foreign exchange receipts. Over 90% of government tax revenue comes from import duties and tourism-related taxes. </p>
      <p>The development of tourism fostered the overall growth of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Maldives" title="Economy of the Maldives">country's economy</a>. It created direct and indirect employment and income generation opportunities in other related industries. The first tourist resorts were opened in 1972 with Bandos Island Resort and Kurumba Village (the current name is Kurumba Maldives),<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> which transformed the Maldives economy. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Landaa_Giraavaru_vue_du_ciel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Landaa_Giraavaru_vue_du_ciel.JPG/220px-Landaa_Giraavaru_vue_du_ciel.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Landaa_Giraavaru_vue_du_ciel.JPG/330px-Landaa_Giraavaru_vue_du_ciel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Landaa_Giraavaru_vue_du_ciel.JPG/440px-Landaa_Giraavaru_vue_du_ciel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3890" data-file-height="2850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Landaa_Giraavaru_vue_du_ciel.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Resort_island" title="Resort island">resort island</a> of <a href="/wiki/Landaa_Giraavaru" title="Landaa Giraavaru">Landaa Giraavaru</a> (Baa atoll)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Tourism_(Maldives)" title="Ministry of Tourism (Maldives)">Ministry of Tourism</a>, the emergence of tourism in 1972 transformed the economy, moving rapidly from dependence on fisheries to tourism. In just three and a half decades, the industry became the main source of income. Tourism was also the country's biggest foreign currency earner and the single largest contributor to the GDP. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 89 resorts in the Maldives offered over 17,000 beds and hosted over 600,000 tourists annually.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In 2019 over 1.7 million visitors came to the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The number of resorts increased from 2 to 92 between 1972 and 2007. As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, over 8,380,000 tourists had visited Maldives.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country has <a href="/wiki/List_of_mosques_in_the_Maldives" title="List of mosques in the Maldives">six heritage Maldivian coral mosques</a> listed as <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> tentative sites.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Visitors">Visitors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Visitors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Maldives#Transportation" title="Maldives">Maldives §&nbsp;Transportation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Visa_policy_of_Maldives" title="Visa policy of Maldives">Visa policy of Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Visitors to the Maldives do not need to apply for a visa pre-arrival, regardless of their country of origin, provided they have a valid passport, proof of onward travel, and the money to be self-sufficient while in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-doi_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doi-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most visitors arrive at <a href="/wiki/Velana_International_Airport" title="Velana International Airport">Velana International Airport</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Hulhul%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Hulhulé">Hulhulé</a> Island, adjacent to the capital Malé. The airport is served by flights to and from India, Sri Lanka, <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, Singapore, Istanbul, and major airports in South-East Asia, as well as charters from Europe. <a href="/wiki/Gan_International_Airport" title="Gan International Airport">Gan Airport</a>, on the southern atoll of <a href="/wiki/Addu_City" title="Addu City">Addu</a>, also serves an international flight to <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> several times a week. <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> offers direct flights to the Maldives around 2–3 times per week.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fishing_industry">Fishing industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Fishing industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry_in_the_Maldives" title="Fishing industry in the Maldives">Fishing industry in the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Doni_aux_Maldives_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Doni_aux_Maldives_cropped.jpg/220px-Doni_aux_Maldives_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Doni_aux_Maldives_cropped.jpg/330px-Doni_aux_Maldives_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Doni_aux_Maldives_cropped.jpg/440px-Doni_aux_Maldives_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1498" data-file-height="1069"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Doni_aux_Maldives_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A mechanised traditional inter-island dhoni stripped of its sails
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>For many centuries the Maldivian economy was entirely dependent on fishing and other <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">marine</a> products. Fishing remains the main occupation of the people and the government gives priority to the fisheries sector. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mechanisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechanisation">mechanisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Traditional_fishing_boat" title="Traditional fishing boat">traditional fishing boat</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Dhoni_(fishing_vessel)" title="Dhoni (fishing vessel)">dhoni</a></i> in 1974 was a major milestone in the development of the fisheries industry. A fish canning plant was installed on <a href="/wiki/Felivaru" class="mw-redirect" title="Felivaru">Felivaru</a> in 1977, as a joint venture with a Japanese firm. In 1979, a Fisheries Advisory Board was set up with the mandate of advising the government on policy guidelines for the overall development of the fisheries sector. Manpower development programmes began in the early 1980s, and fisheries education was incorporated into the school curriculum. <a href="/wiki/Fish_aggregating_device" title="Fish aggregating device">Fish aggregating devices</a> and navigational aids were located at various strategic points. Moreover, the opening up of the <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a> (EEZ) of the Maldives for fisheries has further enhanced the growth of the fisheries sector. </p>
      <p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, fisheries contributed over 15% of the country's GDP and engaged about 30% of the country's workforce. Fisheries were also the second-largest foreign exchange earner after <a href="#Tourism">tourism</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Maldives" title="Demographics of the Maldives">Demographics of the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

          </div></td>

      </table>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Population_estimates_of_Maldives.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Population_estimates_of_Maldives.png/220px-Population_estimates_of_Maldives.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Population_estimates_of_Maldives.png/330px-Population_estimates_of_Maldives.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Population_estimates_of_Maldives.png/440px-Population_estimates_of_Maldives.png 2x" data-file-width="1043" data-file-height="775"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Population_estimates_of_Maldives.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Demographics of the Maldives, from 2000 to 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Year </th>

      </table> 
      <p>The largest ethnic group is <a href="/wiki/Dhivehis" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhivehis">Dhivehin</a>, i.e. the Maldivians, native to the historic region of the Maldive Islands comprising today's Republic of Maldives and the island of <a href="/wiki/Minicoy" title="Minicoy">Minicoy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lakshadweep" title="Lakshadweep">Union territory of Lakshadweep</a>, India. They share the same culture and speak the <a href="/wiki/Dhivehi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhivehi language">Dhivehi language</a>. They are principally an <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_peoples" title="Indo-Aryan peoples">Indo-Aryan</a> people, having traces of Middle Eastern, South Asian, <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian</a> and African genes in the population. </p>
      <p>In the past, there was also a small <a href="/wiki/Tamils" title="Tamils">Tamil</a> population known as the <a href="/wiki/Giraavaru_people" title="Giraavaru people">Giraavaru people</a>. This group have now been almost completely absorbed into the larger Maldivian society but were once native to the island of <a href="/wiki/Giraavaru_(Kaafu_Atoll)" title="Giraavaru (Kaafu Atoll)">Giraavaru (Kaafu Atoll)</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This island was evacuated in 1968 due to heavy erosion of the island. </p>
      <p>Some social stratification exists on the islands. It is not rigid, since rank is based on varied factors, including occupation, wealth, Islamic virtue, and family ties. Instead of a complex <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">caste</a> system, there was merely a distinction between noble (bēfulhu) and common people in the Maldives. Members of the social elite are concentrated in Malé. </p>
      <p>The population doubled by 1978, and the <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a> rate peaked at 3.4% in 1985. At the 2006 census, the population had reached 298,968,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> although the census in 2000 showed that the population growth rate had declined to 1.9%. Life expectancy at birth stood at 46 years in 1978, and later rose to 72. Infant mortality has declined from 12.7% in 1977 to 1.2% today, and adult literacy reached 99%. Combined school enrolment reached the high 90s. The population was projected to have reached 317,280 in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2014 Population and Housing Census listed the total population in Maldives as 437,535: 339,761 resident Maldivians and 97,774 resident foreigners, approximately 16% of the total population. However, it is believed that foreigners have been undercounted.<sup id="cite_ref-Maldives_Population_Projections_2014-2054_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maldives_Population_Projections_2014-2054-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prb-maldives_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prb-maldives-130">[130]</a></sup> As of May 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there are 177,585 expatriate workers, out of which 63,000 are estimated to be undocumented in the Maldives: 3,045 Chinese, 3,544 Nepalese, 14,311 Sri Lankans, 24,379 Indians, and 112,158 <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshis_in_the_Maldives" title="Bangladeshis in the Maldives">Bangladeshis</a>, making them the largest group of foreigners working in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Other immigrants include <a href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_the_Maldives" title="Filipinos in the Maldives">Filipinos in the Maldives</a> as well as various Western foreign workers. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Maldives" title="Islam in the Maldives">Islam in the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_of_Hulhumal%C3%A9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Mosque_of_Hulhumal%C3%A9.jpg/220px-Mosque_of_Hulhumal%C3%A9.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Mosque_of_Hulhumal%C3%A9.jpg/330px-Mosque_of_Hulhumal%C3%A9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Mosque_of_Hulhumal%C3%A9.jpg/440px-Mosque_of_Hulhumal%C3%A9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="669"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_of_Hulhumal%C3%A9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mosque in <a href="/wiki/Hulhumal%C3%A9" title="Hulhumalé">Hulhumalé</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the long <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_the_Maldives" title="Buddhism in the Maldives">Buddhist period of Maldivian history</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Muslim traders introduced Islam. Maldivians converted to Islam by the mid-12th century. The islands have had a long history of <a href="/wiki/Sufi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi">Sufic</a> orders, as can be seen in the history of the country such as the building of tombs. They were used until as recently as the 1980s for seeking the help of buried <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">saints</a>. They can be seen next to some old mosques and are considered a part of Maldives's <a href="/wiki/Cultural_heritage" title="Cultural heritage">cultural heritage</a>. </p>
      <p>Other aspects of <a href="/wiki/Tassawuf" class="mw-redirect" title="Tassawuf">tassawuf</a>, such as ritualised <a href="/wiki/Dhikr" title="Dhikr">dhikr</a> ceremonies called Maulūdu (<a href="/wiki/Mawlid" title="Mawlid">Mawlid</a>)—the <a href="/wiki/Liturgy" title="Liturgy">liturgy</a> of which included recitations and certain supplications in a melodic tone—existed until very recent times. These Maulūdu festivals were held in ornate tents specially built for the occasion. At present Islam is the official religion of the entire population, as adherence to it is required for citizenship. </p>
      <p>According to Moroccan traveller <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Battuta" title="Ibn Battuta">Ibn Battuta</a>, the person responsible for this conversion was a Sunni Muslim visitor named Abu al-Barakat Yusuf al-Barbari, sailing from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. He is also referred to as <a href="/wiki/Tabrizugefaanu" class="mw-redirect" title="Tabrizugefaanu">Tabrizugefaanu</a>. His venerated tomb now stands on the grounds of Medhu Ziyaaraiy, across the street from the Friday Mosque, or <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9_Friday_Mosque" title="Malé Friday Mosque">Hukuru Miskiy</a>, in Malé. Built in 1656, this is the country's oldest mosque. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_language" title="Maldivian language">Maldivian language</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dhivehiscript.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Dhivehiscript.svg/220px-Dhivehiscript.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Dhivehiscript.svg/330px-Dhivehiscript.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Dhivehiscript.svg/440px-Dhivehiscript.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="58" data-file-height="36"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dhivehiscript.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Thaana script
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The official and common language is <a href="/wiki/Dhivehi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhivehi language">Dhivehi</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan language</a> closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Sinhala_language" title="Sinhala language">Sinhala language</a> of Sri Lanka. The first known script used to write Dhivehi is the <i><a href="/wiki/Eveyla_akuru" class="mw-redirect" title="Eveyla akuru">eveyla akuru</a></i> script, which is found in historical recording of kings (<i>raadhavalhi</i>). Later a script called <i><a href="/wiki/Dhives_akuru" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhives akuru">dhives akuru</a></i> was used for a long period. The present-day script is called <a href="/wiki/Thaana" title="Thaana">Thaana</a> and is written from right to left. Thaana is said to have been introduced by the reign of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Thakurufaanu_Al_Auzam" title="Muhammad Thakurufaanu Al Auzam">Mohamed Thakurufaanu</a>. </p>
      <p>English is widely spoken by the locals of the Maldives.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Following the nation's opening to the outside world, the introduction of English as a medium of instruction at secondary and tertiary level of education, and its government's recognition of the opportunities offered through tourism, English has now firmly established itself in the country. As such, the Maldives are quite similar to the countries in the Gulf region (cf. Randall &amp; Samimi, 2010; Boyle, 2012). The nation is undergoing vast societal change, and English is part of this.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> </p>
