      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Maldives" title="Culture of the Maldives">Culture of the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_cuisine" title="Maldivian cuisine">Maldivian cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_folklore" class="mw-redirect" title="Maldivian folklore">Maldivian folklore</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2011</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maahefun_Fuvahmulah.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Maahefun_Fuvahmulah.JPG/220px-Maahefun_Fuvahmulah.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Maahefun_Fuvahmulah.JPG/330px-Maahefun_Fuvahmulah.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Maahefun_Fuvahmulah.JPG/440px-Maahefun_Fuvahmulah.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="2136"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maahefun_Fuvahmulah.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Maahefun Festival in <a href="/wiki/Fuvahmulah" title="Fuvahmulah">Fuvahmulah</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The culture of the Maldives is influenced by the cultures of the people of different ethnicities who have settled on the islands throughout the times. </p>
      <p>Since the 12th century AD, there were also influences from <a href="/wiki/Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabia">Arabia</a> in the language and culture of the Maldives because of the conversion to Islam and its location as a crossroads in the central Indian Ocean. This was due to the long trading history between the far east and the middle east. </p>
      <p>Reflective of this is the fact that the Maldives has had the highest national divorce rate in the world for many decades. This, it is hypothesised, is due to a combination of liberal Islamic rules about divorce and the relatively loose marital bonds that have been identified as common in non- and semi-sedentary peoples without a history of fully developed agrarian property and kinship relations.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Maldives" title="Transport in the Maldives">Transport in the Maldives</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_Maldives" title="List of airports in the Maldives">List of airports in the Maldives</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mal%C3%A9_im_Landeanflug.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mal%C3%A9_im_Landeanflug.jpg/220px-Mal%C3%A9_im_Landeanflug.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mal%C3%A9_im_Landeanflug.jpg/330px-Mal%C3%A9_im_Landeanflug.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mal%C3%A9_im_Landeanflug.jpg/440px-Mal%C3%A9_im_Landeanflug.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3411" data-file-height="1876"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mal%C3%A9_im_Landeanflug.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Velana International Airport
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TMA_Terminal.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/TMA_Terminal.JPG/220px-TMA_Terminal.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/TMA_Terminal.JPG/330px-TMA_Terminal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/TMA_Terminal.JPG/440px-TMA_Terminal.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TMA_Terminal.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>TMA Terminal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Velana_International_Airport" title="Velana International Airport">Velana International Airport</a> is the principal gateway to the Maldives; it is near the capital city <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9" title="Malé">Malé</a> and is surrounded by water. International travel is available on government-owned <a href="/wiki/Island_Aviation_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Aviation Services">Island Aviation Services</a> (branded as Maldivian), which operates to nearly all Maldives domestic airports with several <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Dash_8" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Dash 8">Bombardier Dash 8</a> aircraft, and one <a href="/wiki/A320" class="mw-redirect" title="A320">A320</a> with international service to India, Bangladesh, China, and Thailand. </p>
      <p>In Maldives, there are three main ways to travel between islands: by domestic flight, by <a href="/wiki/Seaplane" title="Seaplane">seaplane</a>, or by boat.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> For several years there were two seaplane companies operating: TMA (<a href="/wiki/Trans_Maldivian_Airways" title="Trans Maldivian Airways">Trans Maldivian Airways</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_Air_Taxi" title="Maldivian Air Taxi">Maldivian Air Taxi</a>, but these merged in 2013 under the name TMA. The seaplane fleet is entirely made up of <a href="/wiki/DHC-6_Twin_Otter" class="mw-redirect" title="DHC-6 Twin Otter">DHC-6 Twin Otters</a>. There is also another airline, <a href="/wiki/Flyme_(Villa_Air)" title="Flyme (Villa Air)">Flyme</a>, which operates using <a href="/wiki/ATR_(aircraft_manufacturer)" title="ATR (aircraft manufacturer)">ATR</a> planes to domestic airports, principally <a href="/wiki/Villa_International_Airport" title="Villa International Airport">Maamigili</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dharavandhoo_Airport" title="Dharavandhoo Airport">Dharavandhoo</a> and some others. <a href="/wiki/Manta_Air" title="Manta Air">Manta Air</a> begins its first scheduled seaplane service. Its seaplane fleet is made up of <a href="/wiki/DHC-6_Twin_Otter" class="mw-redirect" title="DHC-6 Twin Otter">DHC-6 Twin Otter</a> aircraft. In addition to the seaplane service, <a href="/wiki/Manta_Air" title="Manta Air">Manta Air</a> utilizes <a href="/wiki/ATR_(aircraft_manufacturer)" title="ATR (aircraft manufacturer)">ATR 72-600</a> aircraft to operate domestic flights to <a href="/wiki/Dhaalu_Airport" title="Dhaalu Airport">Dhaalu Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dharavandhoo_Airport" title="Dharavandhoo Airport">Dharavandhoo Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kooddoo_Airport" title="Kooddoo Airport">Kooddoo Airport</a> from the main <a href="/wiki/Velana_International_Airport" title="Velana International Airport">Velana International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Depending on the distance of the destination island from the airport, resorts organise <a href="/wiki/Speedboat" class="mw-redirect" title="Speedboat">speedboat</a> transfers or <a href="/wiki/Seaplane" title="Seaplane">seaplane</a> flights directly to the resort island jetty for their guests. Several daily flights operate from <a href="/wiki/Velana_International_Airport" title="Velana International Airport">Velana International Airport</a> to the 12 domestic and international airports in the country. Scheduled ferries also operate from <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9" title="Malé">Malé</a> to many of the atolls. The traditional Maldivian boat is called a <a href="/wiki/Dhoni_(fishing_vessel)" title="Dhoni (fishing vessel)">dhoni</a>. Speedboats and seaplanes tend to be more expensive, while travel by dhoni, although slower, is relatively cheaper and convenient. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maldives&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Maldives_National_University" title="Maldives National University">Maldives National University</a> is one of the country's three institutions of higher education. Its mission statement is as follows: </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p>To create, discover, preserve and disseminate knowledge that is necessary to enhance the lives and livelihoods of people and essential for the cultural, social and economic development of the society so that this nation shall remain free and Islamic forever.<sup id="cite_ref-MNU_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MNU-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>In 1973, the Allied Health Services Training Centre (the forerunner of the Faculty of Health Sciences) was established by the Ministry of Health. The Vocational Training Centre was established in 1974, providing training for mechanical and electrical trades. In 1984, the Institute for Teacher Education was created and the School of Hotel and Catering Services was established in 1987 to provide trained personnel for the tourist industry. In 1991, the Institute of Management and Administration was created to train staff for public and private services. In 1998, the Maldives College of Higher Education was founded. The Institute of Shar'ah and Law was founded in January 1999. In 2000 the college launched its first-degree programme, Bachelor of Arts. On 17 January 2011 the Maldives National University Act was passed by the President of the Maldives; </p>
